# latexd Progress

## Current Status

- Scope: Rust-based partial LaTeX-compatible incremental compiler, following the roadmap in [`README.md`](/home/seorii/dev/hancomac/latexd/README.md).
- Detailed remaining-work backlog: [`docs/work-backlog.md`](/home/seorii/dev/hancomac/latexd/docs/work-backlog.md).
- Detailed `M12` checklist and definition of done: [`docs/m12-checklist.md`](/home/seorii/dev/hancomac/latexd/docs/m12-checklist.md).
- Milestone split: `M11` is tracked as `M11.1`~`M11.4`, and `M12` is tracked as `M12.1`~`M12.6`.
- Current phase: post-`M12` follow-on planning on top of completed `M11` and completed `M12`. The project now has an end-to-end daemon/web preview slice, a project model, dependency-aware rebuild skipping, a tokenizer/interner, a small TeX VM, format snapshots, local `.cls`/`.sty` loading, an internal text layout/PDF pipeline, checkpoint metadata, page-level artifact reuse, a viewport-tile preview path that can run against the mock rasterizer, `gs`, or `libgs`, a line-aware syncmap/click-selection preview path with page-local source/output windows and explicit open-source bridge surfaces, and a semantic aux subsystem that persists concrete artifacts, drives rerun-to-fixpoint, and participates in checkpoint/page reuse.
- `2026-05-15` note: the real-rendering first batch is now implemented and green on `main`. `tex-render-model` owns shared provenance/event/IR/display-list skeleton types, `tex-vm` dual-writes optional `RenderEvent` streams without mutating IR, `tex-layout` builds first-slice `DocumentIr` and text-only `PageDisplayList` pages, and `latexd` can emit event/IR/display-list/PDF/SVG debug artifacts without replacing the legacy PDF path. Recent follow-up commits hardened migrated inline capture for citations, references, links, URL/text wrappers, inline/display math, labels, line breaks, lists, simple environments, tabular fallback text, nested text wrappers, escaped visible characters, nonbreaking spaces, and readable unknown one-argument commands inside text wrappers. The latest pushed commit is `9324dd0` (`feat: capture readable wrapper commands`), and GitHub Actions run `25912613639` passed Web Test and Rust Test.
- `2026-05-20` note: real-rendering event/IR hardening has continued through `5de173a` (`feat: add comment package shim`). The latest slices preserve more common wrapper content without falling back to raw unsupported text: spacing/margin/minipage/multicol/layout wrappers consume non-visible arguments, theorem/algorithm/subequations/appendix wrappers preserve structured body content, `NoHyper` suppresses link annotations while keeping visible text, boxed environments such as `framed`, `shaded`, `tcolorbox`, and `mdframed` hide style options, and `comment`/custom `excludecomment` environments no longer leak non-visible draft text. Local verification for the latest slice passed `cargo test -p tex-vm render_event_capture`, `cargo test -p latexd --test render_ir`, `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, and `git diff --check`; the newest GitHub Actions runs were still in progress when this note was written.
- `2026-05-20` note: the renderer-boundary hardening pass has continued through `a79512e` (`feat: hash raw fallback sources`). The display-list PDF/SVG debug path now carries page/content-hash metadata, text clusters, PDF font family/style resource selection, SVG source provenance for text/image/link/destination ops, optional `pdftotext` extraction coverage for compact display-list PDFs, and stronger content-hash invalidation for text style/link geometry. Raw fallback events now use byte-bounded UTF-8 excerpts plus `blake3:` full-source hashes, and `RawFallbackIr` preserves fallback debug metadata for downstream artifact correlation. Local verification covered `cargo test -p tex-vm`, `cargo test -p tex-render-model`, `cargo test -p tex-layout`, `cargo test -p latexd --test render_ir`, `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, and `git diff --check`; GitHub Actions had passed through `df0f87c` while the newest fallback-related runs were still in progress.
- `2026-05-21` note: render-boundary hardening has continued through `2e82c2f` (`fix: capture optional default link wrappers`). Recent slices preserve normalized graphic asset formats and optional `blake3:` asset hashes from `GraphicRef` through IR into display-list `Image` operations, elide asset hashes in semantic goldens, and add exact provenance coverage for direct input-file headings, cross-file input macro call/definition spans, preamble-input/package/class macro definitions, starred/provided section-wrapper declarations, optional-default section wrappers such as `\newcommand{\mysection}[2][]{\section[#1]{#2}}`, `\def`/`\gdef`-style section wrappers and readable one-argument wrappers, direct `\let` aliases to heading commands, alias chains through user-defined heading/wrapper macros, level-preserving aliases/wrappers for `\subsection` and deeper headings, citation/reference/link/label wrapper macros such as `\newcommand{\mycite}[1]{\cite{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\mycitepair}[2]{\cite{#1,#2}}`, `\newcommand{\papercite}[1]{\cite{paper:#1}}`, `\newcommand{\corecite}{\cite{core}}`, `\newcommand{\defaultcite}[1][default]{\cite{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\myref}[1]{\ref{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\secref}[1]{\ref{sec:#1}}`, `\newcommand{\introref}{\ref{sec:intro}}`, `\newcommand{\defaultref}[1][sec:intro]{\ref{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\mylink}[2]{\href{#1}{#2}}`, `\newcommand{\doclink}[1]{\href{https://constant.test}{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\defaultdoilink}[1][10.1000/default]{\href{https://doi.org/#1}{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\seclabel}[1]{\label{#1}}`, `\newcommand{\templabel}[1]{\label{sec:#1}}`, `\newcommand{\introlabel}{\label{sec:intro}}`, and `\newcommand{\defaultlabel}[1][sec:intro]{\label{#1}}` plus their `\let` aliases, direct `\let` aliases to migrated inline citation/reference/link/label commands, templated link targets such as `\href{https://doi.org/#1}{#1}`, and two-argument reference range wrappers/aliases such as `\newcommand{\myrange}[2]{\crefrange{#1}{#2}}` / `\let\myrange\crefrange`. Local verification for the latest slices passed `cargo test -p tex-vm`, `cargo test -p latexd --test render_ir`, `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, and `git diff --check`; GitHub Actions had passed through `ca8655d` while the newest wrapper runs were still in progress when this note was written.
- `2026-05-15` remaining latexd rendering scope: real TeX page layout/page breaking, serious display-list production, renderer-neutral font resolution and shaping, Skia or other backend integration, external PDF/EPS/SVG asset conversion, strict raster diff, and full arXiv oracle/performance gates remain intentionally outside the current event/IR spike. Near-term implementation should stay on small correctness slices around migrated event capture, IR recovery, provenance, display-list debug artifacts, and compact/default-CI goldens.
- `2026-03-30` note: the recent web packaging pass split the frontend into a `pnpm` workspace, a vanilla-TS `web/packages/viewer-core` library, and a SvelteKit `web/apps/viewer` shell. That work was infrastructure follow-through, not a new milestone.
- `2026-04-06` note: the current compiler-hardening lane is now broad enough that it should no longer be tracked as one long “continue work” stream. The active test-hardening work is now split into smaller compiler batches in [`docs/work-backlog.md`](/home/seorii/dev/hancomac/latexd/docs/work-backlog.md), and `crates/latexd/tests/smoke.rs` is now explicitly treated as an oversize test-host that should be split by family instead of absorbing every new matrix forever.
- `2026-04-09` note: `CH-5` is now actively in progress, not just planned. `crates/latexd/tests/smoke.rs` has been reduced to a small host file with `include!`-based family slices for `external_oracle`, `bibliography_features`, `bibliography_output`, `bibliography`, `reference_variants`, `unchanged_tail`, and `replay_selection`, and the root host is down to roughly `600` lines instead of carrying every smoke family inline.

- `2026-05-07` note: `external_oracle_engine_failures_warning_and_spawn.rs` now uses shared warning/spawn runners for the pdflatex and tectonic warning/spawn leaves. The four leaves are down to `7` lines each from `22/26`, the helper is `149` lines, and all four targeted warning/spawn filters remain green.
- `2026-04-13` note: `bibliography_output.rs` is now a small include host too. Its bibliography-output normalization cases are split into basic-wrapper, punctuation-and-spacing, and textstyle-and-starred leaves; targeted bibliography-output wrapper checks remain green.
- `2026-04-13` note: `bibliography_multi_same_page_trailing_input_included_body_baseline.rs` is now a small include host too. Its included-body same-page trailing-input baseline cases are split into baseline/reversed/follows and precedes/unreadable leaves; targeted replay/fallback exact lanes remain green.
- `2026-04-14` note: `bibliography_multi_same_page_trailing_input_baseline.rs` is now a small include host too. Its same-page trailing-input baseline cases are split into baseline/reversed, untracked-noise, and unreadable-noise leaves; all `6/6` targeted exact replay/fallback checks remain green.
- `2026-04-14` note: `bibliography_multi_same_page_trailing_input_sibling_extra_dirty_untracked.rs` is now a small include host too. Its top-level same-page trailing-input extra-dirty untracked-noise cases are split into dirty-order, interleaved-order, and other-interleaved-order leaves; all `6/6` targeted exact replay/fallback checks remain green.
- `2026-04-14` note: `bibliography_multi_same_page_trailing_input_included_body_sibling_extra_dirty_unreadable.rs` is now a small include host too. Its included-body same-page trailing-input extra-dirty unreadable-noise cases are split into dirty-order, interleaved-order, and other-interleaved-order leaves; all `6/6` targeted exact replay/fallback checks remain green.
- `2026-04-14` note: `bibliography_multi_same_page_trailing_input_included_body_sibling_extra_dirty_untracked.rs` is now a small include host too. Its included-body same-page trailing-input extra-dirty untracked-noise cases are split into dirty-order, interleaved-order, and other-interleaved-order leaves; all `6/6` targeted exact replay/fallback checks remain green.
- Because that packaging work preempted the lane that had already resumed after `M12`, the original post-`M12` follow-on items are still next up:
  - viewer/editor hardening tail, especially stronger external editor integration and the remaining helper/runtime regression gaps around the open-source bridge surface
  - remaining `viewer-core` vs `latexd` app-boundary cleanup that the packaging pass intentionally did not finish yet, especially latexd-specific transport, DTO decoding, hash/global bridge, and host event wiring that still partly live in the core package
  - the broader post-`M12` backlog already called out elsewhere: wider engine-profile hardening, artifact-driven invalidation tightening, and richer renderer/display-list ownership

## Completed Milestones

- `M0`: `latexd` daemon, WebSocket preview protocol, browser viewer, last-good preview retention, mock compiler smoke path.
- `M1`: `00README`/profile/path resolver with arXiv-style root semantics and image resolution.
- `M2`: dependency trace parsing, tracked-input hashing, no-op rebuild short-circuit.
- `M3`: `tex-tokens` + `tex-lexer` with catcodes, control sequence interning, UTF-8 spans, and scanner tests.
- `M4`: `tex-vm` with grouping, `\def`, `\let`, parameterized macros, `\expandafter`, `\csname`, `\ifdefined`, `\ifx`, `\ifnum`, `\count`, `\number`, `\input`, snapshot/restore, and transcript capture.
- `M5`: mini-kernel format snapshot, project runner, local `\documentclass` / `\usepackage` loading, `\newcommand`, and error classification for undefined control sequences / missing files.
- `M6`:
  - `tex-layout` deterministic line/page layout.
  - `tex-pdf` simple valid PDF emission.
  - `tex-bootstrap` project-to-PDF internal build path.
  - `latexd --compiler-bin internal` path with page metadata, dependency trace, and internal compiler smoke tests.
- `M7` initial replay path:
  - `tex-checkpoint` crate with checkpoint bundle metadata.
  - preamble checkpoint + shipout checkpoint bundle serialization.
  - preamble key hashing and previous-revision checkpoint selection.
  - internal compiler writes per-revision `checkpoints.json`.
  - internal compiler reuses a matching preamble snapshot on body-only edits.
  - internal compiler detects unchanged tail alignment against prior shipout checkpoints.
  - internal compiler converts page diffs into `PatchPages` insert/replace/delete ops.
  - internal compiler now persists `output.txt` plus tracked source snapshots per revision.
  - internal compiler now stores actual shipout snapshots with source offsets and can replay from a compatible prior shipout checkpoint for late body edits.
  - `\input`-style non-toplevel sources now carry module output traces into page metadata, so replay selection can also pick later shipout checkpoints for late included-file edits.
  - revision state now persists module output traces alongside source snapshots, and replay selection consults those traces before falling back to coarse page source spans for non-toplevel edits.
  - internal compiler now also persists input-boundary VM snapshots for `\input` sites as first-class checkpoints inside `checkpoints.json`, so late included-file edits can replay from the actual input safe point instead of only approximating via shipout/page metadata.
  - input-boundary checkpoints now persist nested `resume_path + continuation_stack` context plus enter/exit kind, so replay can resume from nested input exits inside changed parent files instead of falling back to a much earlier parent-entry checkpoint.
  - nested replay checkpoint recapture no longer falls back to preamble/full recapture; the compiler now replays only the suffix continuation chain to rebuild shipout checkpoints after a nested input-boundary replay.
- `M8` bootstrap:
  - preview protocol carries `page_ids` plus explicit `page_artifacts` on full-PDF updates.
  - viewer reducer applies `PatchPages` to its page inventory and clamps page navigation to known pages.
  - viewer renders a page stack of per-page PDF iframes and preserves old-vs-new page sources across unchanged tails.
  - internal compiler writes `rev-N/pages/<page_id>.pdf` artifacts for page-level preview.
  - internal compiler also writes `rev-N/pages/<page_id>.svg` artifacts for a lighter-weight custom page viewer path.
  - revision-specific artifact URLs keep old/new PDF pages addressable at the same time.
  - stable page IDs now survive inserted pages before an unchanged tail.
  - internal compiler reuses prior revision page artifacts when page IDs and content hashes still match.
  - `PatchPages` ops now carry per-page artifact URLs, so changed pages can switch immediately without waiting for full-state reconciliation.
- `M9` bootstrap:
  - `tex-render-gs` crate with `Renderer` trait, `MockRenderer`, tile key hashing, viewport→tile planning, and stale tile invalidation tests.
  - `CliRenderer` now shells out to Ghostscript, decodes PNG output, and crops tiles from the rendered page image.
  - `GsApiRenderer` now performs a minimal in-process render by loading `libgs` at runtime and driving `gsapi_init_with_args` with `pngalpha` file output.
  - `latexd` can now provision a reusable `GsApiRuntimePool` for `--tile-renderer gs-api`, so multiple ready runtimes can be reused in round-robin instead of constructing a fresh renderer object for every request.
  - `latexd` now exposes mock full-page PNG, tile PNG, and viewport tile-manifest endpoints backed by saved page metadata.
  - the browser viewer now fetches tile manifests for visible SVG pages and overlays mock PNG tiles on top of each page artifact for viewport-local refresh.
  - `latexd serve` can now choose `--tile-renderer mock`, `--tile-renderer gs-cli`, or `--tile-renderer gs-api`, with page metadata recording the actual per-page PDF artifact path used by the raster backend.
  - `gs-api` mode can now also size a runtime pool via `--gs-api-pool-size`.
  - `latexd` now keeps a revision/page/zoom full-page raster cache, so repeated tile requests for the same visible page reuse one Ghostscript render instead of shelling out on every tile.
  - the viewer now reports `viewport_changed` messages with current page, scroll position, and visible page ids, and the daemon uses them to prewarm raster cache entries in the background.
  - the raster cache is now also persisted as PNG files under the build directory, so server restarts can reuse prior `rev/page/content/zoom` rasters without re-invoking Ghostscript on the first request.
  - concurrent cold misses for the same `rev/page/content/zoom` raster are now deduplicated inside the daemon, so only one render runs while other requests await the shared result.
- `M10` bootstrap:
  - `latexd` now exposes a coarse `/api/syncmap/<rev>/<page_id>` endpoint that converts ordered page `source_spans` into vertical source bands per page.
  - those syncmap bands now also carry revision-stable source line ranges from `sources.json`, and the browser viewer fetches them on demand, ignores stale-revision responses, and surfaces click/hover source selection in the sidebar plus page overlay markers.
  - `latexd` now also exposes a coarse `/api/source-jump/<rev>?file=...&offset=...` lookup, accepts line-based lookup when byte offsets are unavailable, and the viewer installs both `window.latexdJumpToSource(...)` plus hover/select DOM custom-event bridge surfaces for source→preview jumps and preview→source notifications.
  - internal builds now also persist `page-syncmap.json` with page-local output ranges, so syncmap bands can follow actual rendered output slices instead of redistributing page height purely by source-byte proportion when that richer data is available.
  - the viewer now mirrors selected source spans into a `#src=...&line=...` / `#src=...&offset=...` URL hash and can resolve those hash deep-links back through the same source-jump path on load or manual hash changes.
  - the sidebar now exposes an explicit open-source action and emits `latexd:open-source` plus `window.latexdOpenSelectedSource()`, giving an embedding shell/editor a user-driven bridge instead of only passive hover/select notifications.
  - internal `page-syncmap.json` artifacts now split sync spans against per-line text boxes and persist `left/right/top/bottom` geometry, and the viewer uses that geometry for narrower marker overlays plus X/Y-aware nearest-span hit testing instead of treating every sync item as full-width.
  - `latexd serve` can now also take an optional local editor bridge command, exposes `/api/open-source/<rev>`, and when that bridge is configured the preview click path can launch the local editor at the selected line while still keeping the DOM/hash bridge surfaces for embedding shells.
  - the daemon now also exposes `/api/source-file/<rev>?file=...`, and the browser viewer uses it to render an in-browser source pane with highlighted line ranges, preview→source reveal, and source-line click/hover → preview jump, which closes the roadmap's “browser click jumps to source line” bar inside the web UI itself.
- `M11` bootstrap:
  - new `tex-aux` crate with semantic aux IR, parser/writer, semantic equality, and backdating-aware serialization tests.
  - recursive project scan now understands `\section`, `\subsection`, `\subsubsection`, `\label`, `\ref`, `\eqref`, `\pageref`, `\cite`, `\tableofcontents`, `\bibliography`, and `\input` enough to build a minimal semantic view of labels, TOC, citations, and `.bbl` inputs.
  - the semantic aux scaffold now also understands `\nocite{...}` and expands `\nocite{*}` to the current bibliography key set, while materialized sources strip `\nocite` from visible output instead of leaking the control sequence into the rendered text.
  - aux-sensitive internal builds now materialize rewritten sources, ingest `.bbl` files as first-class inputs, and rerun from the base snapshot until the semantic aux IR converges.
  - converged builds now persist `aux.json`, keep `.bbl` files in tracked inputs / `sources.json`, and emit resolved output for `\ref`, `\eqref`, `\pageref`, `\cite`, `\tableofcontents`, and `\bibliography`.
  - converged builds now also persist a concrete `semantic.aux` artifact alongside `aux.json`, and `tex-aux` can round-trip/load either JSON or that concrete aux-style payload for the current semantic subset.
  - that concrete `semantic.aux` payload now leans on real aux-like surface too: `\newlabel`, `\citation`, `\bibdata`, `\bibstyle`, `\bibcite`, and `\@writefile/\contentsline` are emitted for the subset that maps naturally onto classic aux traffic, while richer semantic-only facts continue to use explicit latexd records.
  - the semantic IR now also carries bibliography input/style facts (`\bibdata` / `\bibstyle`-equivalent state), so semantic equality and concrete aux backdating cover more than labels/TOC/citation keys alone.
  - semantically equal aux state can now backdate the previous revision's raw `aux.json` payload instead of always reserializing, and each revision also records `build-meta.json` with aux sensitivity, semantic pass/rerun counts, fixpoint status, and whether aux payload backdating happened.
  - aux-sensitive body edits can now also seed rerun-to-fixpoint from a reusable preamble checkpoint instead of always starting from the mini-kernel snapshot, so the semantic path no longer forces a full preamble replay when CP0 is still valid.
  - `build-meta.json` now also records dirty files, start checkpoint id/page index, and rebuilt-vs-reused page counts, so replay and page reuse behavior is observable per revision instead of only inferred from tests or artifact diffs.
  - aux-sensitive converged builds now also run unchanged-tail alignment against the prior revision again, so semantic reruns can still carry forward tail checkpoint metadata and emit empty page patches / full page-artifact reuse when the final output did not actually move.
  - revision `sources.json` now persists both raw tracked files and separately materialized `executed_files`, so aux-sensitive replay selection and checkpoint rebasing can compare against the rewritten source that actually ran instead of only the on-disk TeX text.
  - semantic builds now also persist `semantic-index.json`, a file-grouped summary of labels, TOC entries, citation keys, bibliography keys, extracted bibliography identifiers (`url` / `doi` / `eprint`), and any extra persisted `\bibinfo{field}{value}` pairs, so aux/debug state is inspectable without re-deriving meaning from raw `aux.json` alone.
  - semantically equal late `.bbl` edits can now replay from the persisted bibliography input-boundary checkpoint instead of falling back to CP0, so bibliography-only aux churn no longer forces a preamble restart once the final rendered output is unchanged.
  - the replay selector now also treats rewritten executed-source diffs as first-class dirty inputs during aux-sensitive builds, so a `.bbl` change that renumbers an earlier `\cite` falls back to CP0 instead of replaying too late from the bibliography input boundary.
  - replay selection now keeps raw-source diffs and executed-source override diffs in separate coordinate spaces; override-only dirty files use conservative safe points instead of comparing rewritten output offsets against raw-source checkpoint offsets.
  - `sources.json` now also persists semantic `rewrite_spans`, and replay selection remaps override-only semantic diffs onto materialized-source checkpoint coordinates as well as raw-source coordinates, so same-page bibliography/input boundaries no longer win just because rewritten source got shorter than the raw TeX around it.
  - the semantic aux scaffold now also accepts `\ref*` / `\eqref*` / `\pageref*`, citation commands with optional note arguments like `\cite[...]{...}`, and `.bbl` entries that use `\bibitem[...]{...}` optional labels, with internal compiler smoke coverage for the full path.
  - numeric citation rewrites no longer drop optional notes: `\cite[pre][post]{...}` now materializes those notes into the rendered citation text instead of silently collapsing everything to the bare citation number.
  - section numbering and TOC derivation now extend through `\subsubsection`, so semantic aux label numbering can resolve nested section references like `1.1.1` instead of flattening everything at subsection depth.
  - optional section titles like `\section[Short]{Long}` now use the short form for TOC entries while materialized executed source keeps the long title in body output, so the current scaffold no longer has to choose between readable text and stable TOC semantics.
  - `\nameref` now prefers the raw scanned long heading title even when TOC derivation keeps a separate short title, so `\section[Short]{Long}` no longer collapses title-based refs down to the TOC shorthand.
  - starred section forms like `\section*{Prelude}` are now materialized as body text but excluded from TOC/section numbering, so unnumbered headings no longer leak raw control sequences into aux-sensitive builds.
  - bibliography numbering now preserves the first-seen `\bibliography{...}` stem order across multiple `.bbl` files instead of silently re-sorting by filename, so semantic cite numbers match document order in multi-file bibliography setups.
  - bibliography cleanup now treats `\href{url}{label}` as visible label text instead of leaking the raw URL target into executed `.bbl` output, which makes common hyperref-heavy bibliography entries much less noisy in the current scaffold.
  - semantic aux project scan now follows `\include{...}` in addition to `\input{...}`, and the mini-kernel maps `\include` back onto the existing input primitive, so chapter-style splits participate in TOC/label/citation derivation instead of being invisible to the current scaffold.
  - that split-document scaffold now also honors `\includeonly{...}` in both semantic scan and the internal VM execution path, so excluded `\include` files stop leaking into TOC/labels/output just because the project is split across chapter files.
  - manual TOC entries via `\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{...}` are now tracked as unnumbered TOC items, and `\phantomsection` / `\addcontentsline` are stripped from executed source output, so starred headings can participate in the TOC without leaking aux-only commands into the preview text.
  - the current semantic aux rewrite also resolves `\nameref` / `\nameref*` against the nearest preceding heading or float caption title, so section refs keep meaningful titles and figure/table/algorithm labels can now resolve to caption text instead of falling back to the surrounding section heading.
  - equation labels now have a minimal semantic counter too: labels attached to `\begin{equation}...\label{...}\end{equation}` are numbered by equation order instead of inheriting the surrounding section number or raw label index, so `\eqref` can at least point at equation-local numbers in the common single-counter case.
  - common sub-reference surface is scaffolded too: `\subref` and `\subeqref` now materialize through the same semantic label map instead of leaking raw commands into executed source.
  - that equation awareness now also flows through `\autoref`, `\cref`, `\namecref`, `\vref`, and `\crefrange`, so equation labels stop falling back to `Section`/`section` wording in the common cross-reference variants.
  - the same minimal counter now also treats common equation-like amsmath environments such as `align`, `gather`, `multline`, and `eqnarray` as equation sources, so those labels use equation-local numbering and equation-kind references too.
  - figure/table labels now have equally minimal semantic counters too, so labels attached under `figure` and `table` stop inheriting section numbers and can flow through `\autoref`, `\cref`, `\namecref`, and `\vref` as `Figure` / `Table` instead of section fallbacks.
  - the same float-style scaffold now also treats `algorithm` as its own numbered label kind, so common algorithm-package references can materialize as `Algorithm 1` / `algorithm` instead of collapsing back to section wording.
  - theorem-like environments now have an equally minimal scaffold too: `theorem`, `lemma`, `proposition`, `corollary`, `definition`, `remark`, `claim`, `example`, `assumption`, `conjecture`, `axiom`, `fact`, `observation`, `problem`, `exercise`, `question`, and `notation` labels use per-kind counters and can flow through `\autoref`, `\cref`, `\namecref`, and `\vref` as `Theorem` / `Claim` / `Problem` / ... instead of falling back to section wording.
  - those theorem-like blocks are now also materialized as visible headings in executed source (`Theorem 1.`, `Lemma 1.`, ...), `proof` environments rewrite to plain `Proof.` text, and titled theorem blocks can drive `\nameref` off the local block title instead of the surrounding section heading.
  - custom theorem definitions now participate in that same scaffold too: `\newtheorem{env}{Display}` environments materialize visible theorem headings instead of leaking raw wrappers, shared-counter forms like `\newtheorem{subenv}[baseenv]{Display}` now advance the same semantic counter group as the referenced base environment, section-scoped forms like `\newtheorem{env}{Display}[section]` now reset under the active heading number instead of flattening back to a global counter, and builtin-name overrides like `\newtheorem{theorem}{Theorem}[section]` now beat the hard-coded fallback so downstream shared environments inherit the overridden scope instead of silently staying global.
  - common `amsthm` declaration commands now stay out of executed source too: `\theoremstyle{...}`, `\newtheoremstyle{...}{...}`, and `\swapnumbers` are treated as non-visible setup instead of leaking raw declarations into semantic-aux builds that already rewrite theorem environments.
  - theorem-style package ref surface is scaffolded too: `\thmref` / `\Thmref` now resolve through the same semantic kind+number path instead of leaking raw commands when theorem-family labels are referenced.
  - composite title-bearing ref surface is scaffolded too: `\fullref` / `\Fullref` now combine kind, number, and nearest semantic title (`Section 1 (Intro)`, `Theorem 1 (Pythagoras)`, ...) instead of leaking raw commands in aux-sensitive documents.
  - title-only ref surface now also rides the same semantic title path: `\titleref` / `\Titleref` resolve to the nearest section/caption/theorem title instead of leaking raw commands in aux-sensitive documents.
  - float captions now participate in semantic aux state too: `\caption[Short]{Long}` and `\captionof{figure|table|algorithm}[Short]{Long}` are scanned into persisted caption entries, materialized as `Figure 1: Long`, and can drive `\listoffigures`, `\listoftables`, and `\listofalgorithms` without leaving raw commands behind; starred caption forms stay body-only and no longer leak into float lists, and float-list/caption documents now correctly enter the semantic aux path instead of falling back to raw VM diagnostics.
  - the same semantic rewrite now also strips common float/equation environment wrappers (`figure`, `table`, `algorithm`, `equation`, `align`, `gather`, ...) from executed source instead of leaving raw `\begin{...}` / `\end{...}` control text around already-materialized captions and references.
  - natbib alias surface is scaffolded too: `\defcitealias`, `\citetalias`, and `\citepalias` now round-trip through semantic aux state instead of leaking raw commands, so alias text participates in executed output and aux equality/backdating as well.
  - appendix switching also accepts `\appendices` now, so class/package variants that use that synonym still enter appendix letter numbering and do not leak the raw command into executed output.
  - section-oriented `\autoref` / `\autoref*` plus `\cref` / `\Cref` now rewrite to `Section <number>` in executed source and final output, so the common hyperref/cleveref cross-reference surface no longer falls through as raw control sequences in this scaffold.
  - `.bbl` optional `\bibitem[...]` labels now also feed `\citeauthor` / `\citeyear` rewriting, so author/year citation variants can render from the same semantic bibliography scaffold instead of being left as raw commands.
  - natbib starred author variants now actually differ from the base forms when the optional `\bibitem[...]` label carries a trailing full-author list (`Short et al.(2024)Full Author List`): `\citeauthor*`, `\citet*`, `\citep*`, `\citealt*`, `\citealp*`, and `\Textcite*` can use that full-author tail instead of collapsing back to the short author form.
  - capitalized author/year variants are covered too: `\Citeauthor` / `\Citeyear` follow the same semantic bibliography path and capitalize the rendered author/year surface instead of leaking raw commands.
  - natbib-like textual citation variants now diverge from the numeric path inside the scaffold: `\citet` renders `Author (Year)` and `\citealt` / `\citealp` / `\onlinecite` render `Author Year` when `.bbl` optional labels provide enough information, with end-to-end smoke coverage through the internal compiler.
  - natbib parenthetical author/year variants are no longer stuck on the numeric cite path either: `\citep` / `\Citep` now use the same semantic bibliography labels to render `(Author, Year)`-style output, while still falling back conservatively when author/year metadata is missing.
  - full-author and year-parenthetical natbib surface is slightly wider too: `\citefullauthor` / `\Citefullauthor` now read the same short-vs-full author metadata path used by starred author variants, and `\Citeyearpar` rides the existing year-only semantic rewrite instead of leaking raw commands.
  - heading-only bibliography surface is scaffolded too: `\printbibheading[heading=bibintoc|bibnumbered,title=...]` now participates in the same bibliography-heading scan/rewrite path as `\printbibliography`, so heading-only bibliography docs still enter the semantic aux path and no longer leak the raw command in executed output.
  - semantic observability now records that surface explicitly too: `semantic-index.json` exposes whether a revision used bibliography-heading semantics, so heading-only bibliography docs can be distinguished from plain TOC/citation cases without re-deriving scan facts.
  - wrapper-style natbib text surface is slightly wider too: `\citetext{...}` now recursively rewrites nested citation commands inside its body and materializes to parenthesized visible text instead of leaking the wrapper or its nested `\cite...` commands into executed output.
  - BibTeX/natbib year-suffix cleanup is slightly more realistic too: `\natexlab{a}` / `\NAT@exlab{b}` are now normalized inside optional citation labels, named bibliography fields, and rendered bibliography text, so year-only semantic refs and full bibliography output can carry `2024a` / `2023b` without leaking the raw suffix wrapper markup.
  - capitalized textual citation variants are scaffolded too: `\Citet`, `\Citealt`, `\Citealp`, and `\Textcite` now capitalize the rendered citation surface instead of behaving identically to the lowercase forms.
  - those textual natbib variants now also preserve optional note arguments, so `\citet[pre][post]{...}` and `\citealt[pre][post]{...}` no longer discard the note payload while rewriting.
  - year-only natbib variants now also work in the same path: `\citeyear` and `\citeyearpar` can preserve year suffixes like `2024a` / `2023b` from optional `\bibitem[...]` labels instead of truncating everything back to a four-digit year.
  - biblatex-flavored common surface is now on the same scaffold too: `\textcite`, `\parencite`, `\autocite`, `\footcite`, `\addbibresource`, and `\printbibliography` all materialize without leaking raw commands, and `\printbibliography[heading=bibintoc|bibnumbered,title=...]` now contributes both TOC structure and visible heading text.
  - that biblatex citation surface now also covers `\smartcite` / `\smartcites`, keeping them on the same semantic author/year parenthetical path instead of leaving another common biblatex command family raw in executed output.
  - numeric biblatex superscript-style citation surface is scaffolded too: `\supercite` / `\supercites` now rewrite to a conservative plain-text `^...` form instead of leaking raw commands into executed output.
  - full-entry bibliography references are now covered too: `\fullcite`, `\footfullcite`, and `\bibentry` materialize directly from the semantic bibliography text instead of leaking the raw command names into executed source or preview output.
  - biblatex multi-cite surface is now also wired into the same scaffold: `\cites`, `\parencites`, `\autocites`, `\footcites`, and `\textcites` parse repeated note/key groups, feed semantic citation discovery, and materialize to stable executed-source text with internal compiler smoke coverage.
  - numbered bibliography headings are now internally consistent too: `\printbibliography[heading=bibnumbered,title=...]` reuses the derived TOC numbering in body materialization, so executed source, aux TOC, and final preview all agree on the same numbered heading text.
  - `\appendix` now flips section numbering into appendix letters (`A`, `A.1`, ...), is stripped from executed source output, and propagates through both section-style and chapter-style TOC/label derivation plus internal compiler smoke coverage.
  - chapter-style section trees are now part of the same scaffold: `\chapter` participates in TOC/label numbering (`1`, `1.1`, `1.1.1`, ...), is materialized into body text like the other heading commands, and has end-to-end smoke coverage through the internal compiler path.
  - heading depth now also extends through `\paragraph` / `\subparagraph`, so `\autoref` / `\cref` can distinguish `Paragraph 1.1.1.1` and `Subparagraph 1.1.1.1.1` instead of flattening everything past subsubsection depth.
  - `\autoref` / `\cref` rewriting is now less section-only: chapter labels render as `Chapter <n>`, appendix labels render as `Appendix <n>`, and multi-label `\cref{a,b}` lists can at least pluralize same-kind references or fall back to mixed `Section ...; Appendix ...` output instead of treating every label like a single section ref.
  - cleveref-style kind-name refs now have a minimal scaffold too: `\namecref`, `\nameCref`, and `\lcnamecref` materialize heading-kind words (`section`, `Subsection`, `subsubsection`, ...) instead of leaking raw commands into executed source.
  - that same kind-name scaffold now also covers plural cleveref forms: `\namecrefs`, `\nameCrefs`, and `\lcnamecrefs` can render same-kind plurals (`Paragraphs`) or conservative mixed-kind lists (`section; subsection`) without leaking raw commands.
  - cleveref label-only surfaces are scaffolded too: `\labelcref` now emits just the label part (including equation-style `(n)` formatting) and `\labelcpageref` emits bare page numbers, so those wrappers no longer leak raw commands into executed source.
  - range-style cleveref refs now also have a minimal scaffold: `\crefrange` / `\Crefrange` can render heading-kind ranges like `Subsections 1.1 to 1.2` and `Paragraphs 1.2.1.1 to 1.2.1.1.1` through the same semantic label/TOC path.
  - page-oriented ref surface is now partially scaffolded too: `\cpageref`, `\vpageref`, `\vref`, and `\Vref` no longer leak raw commands, and resolve to conservative `page N` / `<kind> <number> on page N` text using the same semantic label/page map.
  - that same page-oriented scaffold now also covers `\Cpageref`, so beginning-of-sentence page refs can capitalize the leading `Page` without falling back to raw control text.
  - that page-oriented surface now also covers `\autopageref`, so another common hyperref page-ref command no longer falls through as raw control text in executed output.
  - simple page-range refs are now scaffolded too: `\pagerefrange{a}{b}` materializes to `pages N to M`, which covers another common aux-driven page-reference surface without leaving the raw command in executed output.
  - varioref range surface is scaffolded too: `\vpagerefrange` now resolves to a bare page range and `\vrefrange` / `\Vrefrange` resolve to conservative `<kind> <number> on page N to ...` text instead of leaking raw commands.
  - cleveref page-range wrappers are scaffolded too: `\cpagerefrange` / `\Cpagerefrange` no longer leak raw commands and now resolve to conservative page-range text via the same semantic label/page map.
  - that same cross-reference scaffold now also distinguishes `Section` / `Subsection` / `Subsubsection` for non-appendix heading labels, so nested heading refs no longer flatten every non-chapter target back to plain `Section`.
  - bibliography text cleaning now preserves text inside braces and strips simple formatting commands without dropping the visible words, so common `.bbl` markup like `{...}`, `\emph{...}`, and escaped symbols such as `\&` survive materialization instead of being mangled.
  - title-based bibliography refs are scaffolded too: `\citetitle` / `\Citetitle` now materialize from the semantic bibliography text instead of leaking raw commands into executed source.
  - low-level bibliography field access is scaffolded too: `\citefield{key}{author|year|title|label|text}` now resolves through the same semantic bibliography state instead of leaking raw commands for those common fields.
  - URL-bearing bibliography refs are scaffolded too: `.bbl` ingestion now keeps the first `\href{...}{...}` / `\url{...}` target per entry in semantic aux state, and `\citeurl` plus `\citefield{key}{url}` materialize that URL instead of leaking raw commands.
  - semantic bibliography metadata is a bit richer now: `.bbl` ingestion also keeps the first `\doi{...}` and `\eprint{...}` payload per entry, and `\citefield{key}{doi|eprint}` resolves those identifiers directly from aux state instead of scraping the rendered bibliography text.
  - direct identifier bibliography refs are scaffolded too: `\citedoi`, `\citeeprint`, `\citeisbn`, and `\citeissn` now ride the same semantic bibliography metadata path instead of leaking raw commands for those common identifier lookups.
  - date-oriented bibliography refs are scaffolded too: `\citedate` and `\citeurldate` now resolve against persisted `date` / `urldate` fields (falling back to `year` when only a bare year is known) instead of leaking raw commands.
  - APS/BibTeX-style wrappers are handled a bit better too: `.bbl` ingestion now reads `\bibinfo{author|year|title|doi|eprint}{...}` into semantic aux metadata, `\citetitle` / `\citeauthor` / `\citeyear` / `\citefield{...}` prefer those exact fields when present, and bibliography text cleanup strips the `\bibinfo` wrapper without leaking the field name into visible output.
  - bibliography wrapper cleanup is slightly broader now too: `\urlprefix` is stripped, `\url{...}` contributes its visible payload directly during cleanup, and `\bibnamedash` turns into a visible ASCII dash marker, so semantic `\fullcite` / `\bibentry` output keeps the intended bibliography text without wrapper commands leaking through.
  - common biblatex text wrappers are now unwrapped conservatively too: `\mkbibquote`, `\mkbibparens`, `\mkbibbrackets`, `\mkbibemph`, `\mkbibbold`, `\mkbibitalic`, and `\enquote` no longer leak into semantic bibliography output, so mounted `.bbl` text reads more like its final visible form.
  - bibliography punctuation/unit wrappers are cleaned up too: `\newunit`, `\finentry`, `\addspace`, `\addcomma`, `\adddot`, `\addcolon`, and `\addsemicolon` now materialize to visible punctuation/spacing instead of leaking wrapper commands or silently dropping separators in `\fullcite` / `\bibentry` output.
  - common biblatex bibliography text wrappers are a bit wider too: `\bibstring{...}`, `\mkbibacro{...}`, and `\mkbibname...{...}` forms including `\mkbibnameaffix{...}` now materialize as visible text instead of leaking wrapper commands inside semantic bibliography output.
  - bibliography spacing/parenthetical wrappers are cleaned up too: `\addabbrvspace`, `\addnbspace`, `\addthinspace`, `\addlowpenspace`, `\addhighpenspace`, and `\parentext{...}` now materialize to visible spacing/parenthesized text instead of leaking wrapper commands in executed bibliography output.
  - bibliography dash/slash wrappers are cleaned up too: `\bibrangedash`, `\textendash`, `\textemdash`, `\addslash`, and `\addhyphen` now materialize to visible ASCII punctuation instead of leaking wrapper commands or collapsing page/title ranges in semantic bibliography output.
  - low-level bibliography punctuation helpers are cleaned up too: `\adddotspace`, `\isdot`, `\nopunct`, `\unspace`, and `\bibopen...` / `\bibclose...` punctuation commands now materialize to conservative visible punctuation/spacing instead of leaking wrapper commands into executed bibliography output.
  - bibliography superscript/subscript/brace wrappers are cleaned up too: `\mkbibsuperscript`, `\mkbibsubscript`, and `\mkbibbraces` now materialize to visible text instead of leaking wrapper commands into semantic bibliography output.
  - URL-like bibliography text wrappers are cleaned up too: `\nolinkurl{...}`, `\path{...}`, and `\detokenize{...}` now contribute their visible payload directly instead of leaking wrapper commands into executed bibliography output.
  - bibliography case/text-style wrappers are cleaned up too: `\protect`, `\relax`, `\leavevmode`, `\ignorespaces`, `\unskip`, `\space`, `\,`, `\;`, `\:`, `\ `, `\!`, `\NoCaseChange`, `\MakeSentenceCase`, `\MakeSentenceCase*`, `\MakeTitleCase`, `\MakeTitleCase*`, `\emph`, `\mbox`, `\hbox`, `\fbox`, `\framebox`, `\raisebox`, `\parbox`, `\makebox`, `\phantom`, `\hphantom`, `\vphantom`, `\textquotesingle`, `\textquotedbl`, `\textless`, `\textgreater`, `\textbar`, `\slash`, `\texttt`, `\textsf`, `\textsc`, `\textbf`, `\textit`, `\textrm`, `\textup`, `\textmd`, `\textnormal`, `\textsuperscript`, and `\textsubscript` now materialize to conservative visible text instead of leaking wrapper commands into executed bibliography output.
  - starred bibliography formatting wrappers are cleaned up too: `\mkbibquote*`, `\mkbibparens*`, `\mkbibbrackets*`, `\mkbibbraces*`, `\mkbibemph*`, `\mkbibbold*`, and `\mkbibitalic*` now follow the same visible-text cleanup path as their non-star variants instead of leaking raw wrapper commands.
  - URL formatting selectors are stripped too: `\urlstyle{...}` now disappears during bibliography cleanup instead of leaking a non-visible style command into executed bibliography output.
  - generic `\bibinfo` field access is scaffolded too: `\citefield{key}{journal|pages|...}` now falls back to any extra `\bibinfo{field}{value}` pairs persisted in semantic aux state instead of being limited to the hard-coded author/year/title/doi/eprint set.
  - numeric natbib surface is one step wider too: `\citenum{...}` now rewrites to the bare bibliography number list instead of leaking raw commands in executed source.
  - `.bbl` wrapper ingestion now also understands `\bibfield{field}{value}`, so the same semantic metadata path used for `\bibinfo` backs `\citeauthor`, `\citeyear`, `\citetitle`, and generic `\citefield{...}` lookups for another common BibTeX/BibLaTeX wrapper family.
  - URL-bearing bibliography metadata also follows that same wrapper path now: `\citeurl` and `\citefield{key}{url}` can resolve `\bibfield{url}{...}` / `\bibinfo{url}{...}` directly instead of only seeing explicit `\href` or `\url` markup inside the `.bbl`.
  - README M11 TDD checklist is now effectively covered by tests:
    - label parse/write roundtrip: covered in `tex-aux`
    - toc equality/backdating: covered in `tex-aux` plus cross-revision aux backdating smoke
    - citation key set equality: covered in `tex-aux`, including `\nocite{*}`
    - `.bbl` ingestion: covered in `tex-aux` and internal compiler smoke
    - rerun until semantic fixpoint: covered in internal compiler smoke and `build-meta.json`
  - extra M11 behavior beyond the README checklist is also in place:
    - previous `aux.json` payloads are backdated byte-for-byte when semantic state is equal
    - previous `semantic.aux` payloads are also backdated byte-for-byte when the concrete aux-style artifact is semantically unchanged
    - aux-sensitive reruns can seed from reusable CP0 instead of always starting at the mini-kernel snapshot
    - bibliography-only semantic churn can replay from persisted input-boundary checkpoints
    - `sources.json` keeps both raw tracked files, the rewritten `executed_files` that actually ran, and the rewrite-span mapping that lets replay convert semantic dirty regions back into checkpoint-local offsets
    - `semantic-index.json` exposes a file-grouped semantic summary for labels/TOC/citations/bibliography plus extracted URL/DOI/eprint identifiers, making semantic state and fixture expectations easier to inspect than the raw aux payload alone
    - semantic builds now expose observability through `build-meta.json` for dirty files, start checkpoint, page reuse, semantic pass count, and fixpoint status
  - practical M11 status:
    - the current subsystem now covers the intended latexd M11 bar: concrete semantic aux artifacts, semantic equality/backdating, rerun-to-fixpoint, checkpoint-seeded aux replay, executed-source persistence, wide common ref/citation/theorem/float surface rewriting, and end-to-end page/checkpoint reuse when final semantic output is unchanged
    - this is now tracked as `M11.1` concrete semantic aux artifact, `M11.2` semantic equality/backdating, `M11.3` rewrite surface, and `M11.4` replay/observability, all complete
    - this means M11 is complete for latexd's intended semantic-aux subsystem, while full LaTeX/package/toolchain compatibility is intentionally deferred to M12 hardening
  - rough M11 completion estimate:
    - README completion bar: 100%
    - intended latexd semantic-aux subsystem bar: 100%
    - full LaTeX/package/toolchain maturity: still substantially incomplete, now explicitly treated as M12 scope

## Current Coverage

- Internal compiler page metadata currently includes:
  - stable `page_id`
  - `content_hash`
  - page dimensions
  - text span in the rendered output
  - lightweight source-span attribution placeholders for toplevel and loaded modules
- Internal compiler now also emits a persisted checkpoint bundle per revision.
- Checkpoint reuse currently validates:
  - dirty-file policy for `00README` / `.cls` / `.sty` / `.cfg` / `.def`
  - current toplevel preamble hash equality before reusing CP0
- Checkpoint metadata now also carries serialized page lists, so the internal compiler can compare the latest revision against prior shipout boundaries and identify an unchanged page tail.
- Checkpoint bundles now also persist shipout snapshots, source offsets, and input-boundary checkpoints; nested input checkpoints now include replay continuation frames, and revision directories keep `output.txt` plus tracked source text snapshots so the compiler can choose a conservative nearest replay checkpoint from prior source/page data.
- Toplevel `.tex` edits now consult saved shipout `source_offset_utf8` boundaries first and clamp them against the page-span dirty region, so late edits can reuse a later checkpoint more reliably without skipping obvious dirty pages.
- Toplevel `.tex` edits now also prefer those saved shipout source offsets over earlier placeholder page spans when the two disagree, so conservative source attribution no longer drags replay all the way back to an older page once a direct checkpoint boundary is available.
- Toplevel `.tex` edits that happen after a previously executed `\input` in the same file can now also reuse the stored input-boundary exit checkpoint for that site, instead of falling all the way back to a shipout or preamble checkpoint when the edit stays on the same page.
- Deleted non-toplevel `\input` files now rewind to the earliest stored enter checkpoint for that module instead of always falling back to the preamble checkpoint, which keeps missing-file rebuilds on a narrower replay window.
- Repeated include instances of the same changed file now use the earliest affected continuation context instead of accidentally preferring the latest occurrence's internal checkpoint, so same-file late edits no longer skip earlier repeated outputs.
- Replay builds now only recapture shipout checkpoints through the dirty middle of the suffix; when an unchanged tail is detected, later shipout snapshots are reused from the prior revision and their persisted `source_offset_utf8` values are rebased onto the current toplevel source before writing the new checkpoint bundle.
- Shipout checkpoints now also persist their `resume_path` and `continuation_stack`, and unchanged-tail reuse rebases those frame offsets path-by-path against the current source snapshot instead of treating every reused shipout as an implicit toplevel-only checkpoint.
- Unchanged-tail shipout reuse now prefers aligned previous/current page-span deltas for each resume/frame path, so later edits elsewhere in the same file no longer force a whole-file offset shift when the reused checkpoint only needs the earlier page-local boundary remap.
- Persisted module traces now also carry file-local `source_start_utf8` / `source_end_utf8`, so replay builds can preserve suffix-only source ranges for resumed inputs and later non-toplevel replay fallback no longer has to map changed offsets across an entire file when only a traced suffix was actually executed.
- Page source-span attribution for loaded modules now uses those persisted trace ranges as well, which keeps replay-generated page metadata aligned with the resumed source slice instead of always stretching each module span across the whole file.
- Page source-span attribution now also subtracts nested input intervals out of parent/toplevel segments before mapping them onto pages, so a page that renders `main -> parent -> child -> parent -> main` output now carries that same ordered span structure instead of one large parent/toplevel placeholder span across the child output.
- The old whole-file source-diff rebasing path was first narrowed to a prefix/suffix-aware remap, so edits after a checkpoint offset no longer moved earlier safe points just because the file grew or shrank later.
- Unchanged-tail shipout rebasing now first tries to locate the persisted module-trace source slice verbatim inside the current source snapshot and uses that exact matched range when it is unique, so safe points inside an unchanged traced suffix survive edits on both sides without depending on a whole-file diff remap.
- Unchanged-tail shipout rebasing now also uses exact module-checkpoint intervals when page spans and module traces are missing, so reused shipout frames no longer need whole-file source-diff remapping just to relocate a safe point inside an unchanged included-file segment.
- Non-toplevel replay fallback now prefers source-ranged module traces over earlier placeholder page spans when both are available, so traced include outputs no longer get pulled back to an overly early page boundary just because source attribution was conservative.
- `latexd` now emits `PatchPages` WebSocket messages from internal builds, and the browser viewer keeps a page inventory synchronized from `page_ids`, `page_artifacts`, and patch ops.
- The viewer now uses server-provided page-artifact URLs directly, so unchanged tail pages can keep the older artifact while inserted/replaced pages switch to the new revision.
- The daemon now serves revision-stable PDF artifact paths under `/artifacts/rev/<rev>/<file>.pdf`, which makes mixed old/new page stacks actually valid.
- The internal compiler also emits page-specific PDF artifacts under `/artifacts/rev/<rev>/pages/<page_id>.pdf`, and the viewer falls back to the full-document iframe when no page inventory is available.
- The internal compiler now emits matching SVG artifacts under `/artifacts/rev/<rev>/pages/<page_id>.svg`, and the viewer prefers those over PDF page embeds for internal builds.
- The compiler now prefers prior revision page artifacts for unchanged pages, so page-level preview reuse is server-driven instead of relying on viewer heuristics alone.
- Changed pages now receive their new PDF/SVG artifact URLs directly inside `PatchPages`, so the viewer can update those pages immediately while unchanged pages stay on prior artifacts.
- `tex-render-gs` now provides the testable tile-planning core needed before actual Ghostscript rectangle rendering is wired.
- `latexd` now persists per-revision page metadata and uses it to serve mock page/tile raster endpoints, so the tile pipeline has a real HTTP surface even before Ghostscript is connected.
- Per-revision page metadata now records the build-relative page-PDF source path, so reused page artifacts from earlier revisions can still be rasterized through the current revision's tile endpoint.
- The browser viewer now consumes tile manifests for visible SVG pages, quantizes viewport requests to tile boundaries, and renders a per-page PNG tile layer over the SVG page background.
- The daemon now reuses cached full-page rasters across both `/pages/*.png` and `/tiles/*` requests at the same zoom bucket, which removes repeated Ghostscript work inside a scrolling session.
- The daemon now also consumes viewer viewport updates and prewarms current/visible page rasters for the current revision, reducing cold tile misses after scroll and page navigation.
- The daemon now reloads disk-backed raster cache files on cold misses, so page/tile requests after a restart can still avoid a Ghostscript render when the build artifacts and zoom bucket match.
- The daemon now also deduplicates concurrent cold misses in front of both memory and disk cache fill, preventing duplicate Ghostscript work when multiple tile/page requests race on the same raster key.
- `tex-render-gs` can now probe a loadable `libgs` shared library at runtime, and both the crate tests and the daemon route tests cover the `gs-api` path on machines where `libgs` is present.
- Renderer/session follow-up is now scoped in [`docs/renderer-session-plan.md`](/home/seorii/dev/hancomac/latexd/docs/renderer-session-plan.md), with actor/session ownership, revision attachment, rectangle-request tiles, and failure/metrics phases split out from M7 work.
- Renderer/session hardening has now started in code as well: the daemon has a shared Phase 1 render actor/session wrapper keyed by document root + renderer mode, so full-page cold misses reuse one renderer lane instead of constructing a fresh renderer path per miss.
- Phase 2 has also started in a broader narrow form: the same actor can now attach/detach recent revision page metadata, answer attached-page lookups before the HTTP handlers fall back to disk metadata, answer full revision page-metadata-set lookups for sync/source-jump style requests, keep a small recent-revision window alive, and expose that attached revision window through the debug surface. Revision retention now follows actor-owned LRU + page-budget eviction instead of build-loop `rev - N` detach, and lookup/render/prewarm paths also refresh attached revision recency.
- Phase 3 has also started in a narrow form: `/tiles/*` requests now go through the same actor/session lane and call renderer-native `render_tiles` instead of rendering a full PNG and cropping it inside the HTTP handler. The actor now also keeps a small rect-tile cache keyed by revision/page/content-hash/zoom/rect, so repeated identical tiles and mixed cached+uncached batches can reuse cached tiles and only render missing rectangles. That cache now also enforces a per-page rect budget on top of the global LRU budget, so one page's rectangle churn does not evict every other page's retained tile ownership. Tile-cache eviction itself is now observable too: the debug snapshot exposes a tile-cache eviction counter and matching `EvictTileCache` events so current rect ownership churn is directly inspectable instead of silently disappearing behind the LRU. The renderer-session debug snapshot now exposes tile-cache entries themselves, not just a count, so current rect ownership and LRU order are directly inspectable. Broader rectangle batching and longer-lived per-page tile/display-list ownership are still follow-up work.
- Phase 5 has also started in a narrow form: the daemon now keeps actor spawn/restart/attach/detach/evict/full-render/tile-render/fallback counters, exposes them through a small debug metrics surface, keeps a recent revision/page keyed event ring for restart/fallback churn, emits matching structured debug logs, records coarse duration for render/tile/fallback events, and treats dead session channels as restart/fallback events instead of silent handle churn. The debug snapshot also now exposes live attached page count, revision-window limit, page-budget context, and actor-owned tile-cache count, while repeated identical tile hits surface as explicit `ReuseTiles` events instead of looking like fresh renderer work.
- Phase 4 has also widened a little further: viewport prewarm still prioritizes current page -> visible pages -> adjacent pages, but the actor-owned warm path now also warms neighboring zoom-step buckets for the current page, keeps a small actor-owned warm-bucket LRU instead of relying on leaked global in-flight claims, exposes those warmed buckets through the debug snapshot, clears stale warmed buckets on detach/evict, and now enforces a per-page zoom-bucket budget so one page's zoom churn does not evict every other warmed page. Immediate zoom-in/out after scroll is less likely to miss cold renderer session state.
- The sync path now also exposes page-local source/output windows directly: `/api/syncmap/<rev>/<page_id>` responses carry `page_source_start_utf8` / `page_source_end_utf8` and `page_output_start_utf8` / `page_output_end_utf8` for both artifact-backed syncmaps and fallback page-metadata derivation, each sync item now also carries item-level `output_start_utf8` / `output_end_utf8` plus a stable `item_id`, artifact/fallback geometry is normalized into page bounds, and the viewer clears stale selection/hover state when a refreshed syncmap shows that the old selection no longer fits inside the new page-local source/output window. If the same `item_id` still exists after a refresh, the viewer now re-anchors the selection/hover to the new geometry and output window instead of dropping it. The viewer runtime now also forwards those fetched page-local source/output windows into reducer state instead of dropping them on the fetch path. `/api/source-jump/<rev>` and `/api/open-source/<rev>` responses now also return the nearest page/item/page-local source-output window plus page geometry and a canonical `source_hash`; when a concrete column is known, that hash now keeps `&column=` instead of collapsing back to line-only links. The viewer prefers that canonical hash for current-page/selected-source state, source links, URL history, and resolved embedding events (`latexd:source-jump-resolved`, `latexd:source-hover-resolved`, `latexd:open-source-resolved`), and `sourceRequestFromSelection(...)` now rehydrates that canonical column when an item has line information but no explicit `startColumn`, so the local editor bridge can round-trip richer selection context without silently falling back to line-only requests. The imperative `window.latexdJumpToSource(...)`, `window.latexdSelectSource(...)`, and `window.latexdHoverSource(...)` helpers now also resolve to that same enriched detail payload instead of raw server JSON, so an embedding shell can reuse the canonical selection/page/item/editor context without separately listening for the resolved DOM events.
- The same editor/sync bridge now also accepts canonical request input directly: `window.latexdJumpToSource(...)`, `window.latexdSelectSource(...)`, and `window.latexdHoverSource(...)` can take `{ sourceHash }` / `{ source_hash }` or plain `"#src=..."` strings, `window.latexdOpenSelectedSource(...)` / `window.latexdPreviewSelectedSource(...)` can take that same direct canonical input, and `latexdOpenSelectedSource(...)` can combine that input with `launch: false` either as a second-arg options object or on the same source-like object. Both `/api/source-jump/<rev>` and `/api/open-source/<rev>` now accept `source_hash`-only request shapes so nested-path and column-precise selections survive another roundtrip without re-deriving them from lossy local fields. The same direct hash/object path now also reconstructs canonical `detail.source` payloads for resolved and failed detail, so embedding shells do not need a separate selected-source-only branch just to recover normalized source identity.
- The editor bridge preview path now also has parity across `source-jump` and `open-source`: both responses return absolute file path, editor cwd, launch-support state, `file_uri`, known-editor `editor_uri`, materialized `editor_program` / `editor_args` / `editor_command_line` previews, and `editor_preview_kind` (`none`, `uri`, `command`, `command_and_uri`) so an embedding shell can inspect or reuse the exact local-editor handoff command or deep-link target no matter which source-resolution path triggered it. `/api/open-source/<rev>` still owns actual launching and directly materializes the same richer context into command placeholders: `{rev}`, `{source_hash}`, `{page_id}`, `{page_index}`, `{page_width}`, `{page_height}`, `{page_source_start}`, `{page_source_end}`, `{page_output_start}`, `{page_output_end}`, `{item_file}`, `{item_start}`, `{item_end}`, `{item_output_start}`, `{item_output_end}`, `{item_id}`, `{editor_program}`, `{editor_command_line}`, `{editor_preview_kind}` are all available there, and the same endpoint still accepts `launch: false` so shells can ask for the fully resolved preview/context payload without actually spawning the local editor process. If a normal open-source request arrives with no configured bridge, the endpoint now also degrades to that same resolved preview payload instead of returning `501`, and the built-in viewer's explicit open-source action now consumes that no-bridge resolved payload instead of stopping at an intent-only local detail object. The viewer now also emits explicit `latexd:source-jump-failed`, `latexd:source-hover-failed`, and `latexd:open-source-failed` events with request/error context so embedding shells can distinguish bridge-preview fallback from actual transport/server failure.
- Corpus realism also moved one larger mixed family up: `split-preamble-mixed-paper-family-workflow` now pins theorem + cleveref + appendix + figure list/caption semantics, bibliography drift, option-only revisions, and nested preamble/package/class/body failure-recovery inside one wrapper-heavy split-preamble project.
- The larger wrapper-heavy paper-family corpus has widened again: `split-preamble-bibliography-heavy-paper-family-workflow` now locks a heavier multi-`.bbl` / `\addbibresource` bibliography lifecycle with order/style drift, semantic-equal vs semantic-change `.bbl`, partial loss/recovery, and preamble/package/class/body failure chains, while `split-preamble-appendix-heavy-paper-family-workflow` does the same for appendix/appendices/theorem/caption/list/reference-heavy semantics. `split-preamble-appendix-reference-paper-family-workflow` and `split-preamble-manual-heading-reference-paper-family-workflow` add two more larger wrapper-heavy families that mix appendix/title/page/range refs and manual-heading/theorem/caption/bibliography stacks under the same partial-loss and failure/recovery chains, `split-preamble-citation-caption-reference-heavy-paper-family-workflow` plus `split-preamble-biblatex-heading-reference-heavy-paper-family-workflow` extend that larger family layer to natbib/biblatex citation stacks with caption/list/title/page/range/reference mixes under the same wrapper-heavy failure/recovery chain, and `split-preamble-manual-heading-caption-reference-heavy-paper-family-workflow` plus `split-preamble-varioref-reference-heavy-paper-family-workflow` now pin the same larger family layer for manual-heading/caption/list/title/page/range refs and `varioref`-heavy theorem/equation/float/title/page/range refs.
- Regression coverage has been strengthened across:
  - VM semantics and diagnostics
  - project runner / internal PDF path
  - page metadata stability
  - checkpoint bundle persistence
  - corpus failure classification via optional `REVN-FAIL-JSON-EXPECT.txt` over `stage` / `subject_kind` / `surface_kind`
  - current failure corpus now carries `FAIL-JSON-EXPECT.txt` end-to-end: split-preamble realistic workflow families, optioned semantic chains, and dedicated diagnostic fixtures all verify `stage` / `subject_kind` / `surface_kind` in addition to substring checks
  - checkpoint preamble-key stability and reuse policy
  - shifted unchanged-tail alignment against prior shipout checkpoints
  - exact trace-slice rebasing for unchanged-tail shipout reuse
  - page patch op planning and protocol roundtrips
  - daemon-side internal compiler smoke paths
  - daemon build-loop no-op warm rebuild skipping
- Diagnostics currently classified:
  - `UndefinedControlSequence`
  - `MissingFile`

## Known Gaps

- No real TeX box/glue/page builder yet. Layout is text-based, fixed-width, and only suitable as an internal scaffold.
- No real LaTeX kernel bootstrap yet. The mini kernel is a handcrafted subset.
- Semantic aux is still a scaffold, not a full LaTeX-compatible aux engine.
  - the current path resolves a narrow set of source commands by materializing rewritten inputs, rerunning to a semantic fixpoint, optionally seeding from a reusable preamble checkpoint, and backdating equal aux payloads across revisions, but it does not model real `.aux` bytecode, BibTeX/Biber execution, package-specific citation styles, or arbitrary TeX macro-generated labels/citations.
- Shipout replay is still conservative. Toplevel edits now use saved shipout source offsets directly and can also reuse same-file `\input` exit checkpoints, while non-toplevel `\input` edits replay from stored input-boundary checkpoints with nested enter/exit continuation frames and source-ranged module traces, but dirty-region selection is still far from a trace-grade VM/input dependency model and repeated include instances are only conservatively grouped by continuation context.
- No true vector/page-layer renderer yet. The viewer now renders a page stack of per-page SVG/PDF artifacts and can overlay viewport tiles on visible pages, but it still relies on simple asset swapping rather than a richer page scene graph.
- No persistent-process Ghostscript adapter yet. `tex-render-gs` now has working `gs-cli` and minimal reusable `gs-api` backends, and latexd caches/deduplicates the resulting rasters in memory and on disk, but both backends still pay `init_with_args`/device setup work for a truly cold miss when neither cache is warm.
- Source attribution is still scaffold-grade rather than true layout-engine sync.
  - It now respects nested input boundaries, output order, page-local output ranges, line-aware box geometry, and an in-browser source pane with revision-stable source fetch, but it is still derived from text spans rather than true box-level sync data from a real TeX layout engine.

## M12 Detail

- `M12` arXiv hardening:
  - completion update: `M12` definition of done is now treated as satisfied, and remaining engine-profile / deeper renderer ownership / stronger external editor integration work is tracked as post-`M12` future scope rather than open `M12` blockers
  - this is now tracked as `M12.1` wrapper-heavy corpus baseline, `M12.2` bibliography/toolchain realism, `M12.3` package/wrapper interaction + semantic artifact tightening, `M12.4` failure/recovery + structured artifact coverage, `M12.5` renderer/session hardening, and `M12.6` sync/editor hardening, all complete
  - start turning README known issues into real regressions and compatibility fixes instead of treating them as post-M11 notes
  - grouped `\usepackage` / `setspace`-style package loading is now fixed and covered: package definitions, including package-side `\input`, stay visible outside the caller group in both `tex-vm` and the internal compiler smoke path
  - `hyperref + hyperxmp`-style package preambles are now fixed and covered: `\RequirePackage` / `\RequirePackageWithOptions` plus common package declaration/setup commands (`\NeedsTeXFormat`, `\ProvidesPackage`, `\PassOptionsToPackage`, `\DeclareOption`, `\ProcessOptions`, `\relax`) no longer leak into output or block local package dependencies in the VM/internal compiler path
  - `revtex + array`-style class chains are now fixed and covered: `\LoadClass` / `\LoadClassWithOptions` plus `\PassOptionsToClass` now let local class wrappers pull in base classes and packages before the document body executes
  - package/class option propagation is now a real narrow VM feature rather than a strip-only scaffold: `\PassOptionsToPackage`, `\PassOptionsToClass`, `\DeclareOption`, `\DeclareOption*`, `\ExecuteOptions`, `\ProcessOptions`, `\ProcessOptions*`, and `\LoadClassWithOptions` now actually propagate and apply declared/default options through local package/class chains, including narrow `\CurrentOption` forwarding in both default-option and declared-option bodies for package and class wrappers
  - `\RequirePackageWithOptions` is now also pinned as part of that narrow option path, so wrapper-package options can be forwarded into nested package loads without falling back to a separate `\PassOptionsToPackage` shim
  - the same fix now preserves forwarded options past `\ProcessOptions`, so `\LoadClassWithOptions` and `\RequirePackageWithOptions` still see the wrapper's original passed option list even after the wrapper has already processed its own option bodies
  - `\ExecuteOptions` + explicit option overlap is now deduped on the `\ProcessOptions` path, so a wrapper package/class does not execute the same option body twice when the default option is also passed explicitly
  - `cleveref + hyperref`-style package hooks are now fixed and covered: `\AtBeginDocument` and `\DeclareRobustCommand` can install delayed package definitions before the document body, which is enough for a minimal local `cleveref.sty` wrapper over `hyperref`
  - package/class end-hook helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same local toolchain level: `\AtEndOfPackage` and `\AtEndOfClass` now narrow-store balanced-group token hooks on the active package/class frame and reinject them just before the module end marker, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins those end-hook paths under a later option-only revision
  - document end-hook helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same local toolchain level: `\AtEndDocument` now narrow-stores balanced-group token hooks in snapshot-aware VM state and reinjects them once the main token queue drains, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins class/package/body end-of-document hooks under a later option-only revision
  - starred command declarations are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\newcommand*`, `\renewcommand*`, `\providecommand*`, and `\DeclareRobustCommand*` now follow the same narrow path as their non-starred forms instead of falling through before the target macro, and a dedicated corpus fixture pins that path under a wrapper class/package stack with a later option-only revision
  - optional default arguments on the same command family are now also fixed and covered at that preamble-definition level: `\newcommand`, `\renewcommand`, `\providecommand`, and `\DeclareRobustCommand` now honor LaTeX-style first optional defaults like `[2][default]` instead of treating the default bracket as stray output, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both default and explicit optional-argument paths under a later option-only revision
  - command declaration guards on the same family are now also fixed and covered at that preamble-definition level: `\newcommand` and `\DeclareRobustCommand` now emit explicit diagnostics instead of silently redefining an existing target, `\renewcommand` now emits an explicit diagnostic instead of silently defining a missing target, `\providecommand` keeps its old “leave existing definitions alone” path, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both failure/recovery chains under later revisions
  - expanded/global definition helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\edef` now narrow-expands its body at definition time instead of leaving dynamic control sequences behind, `\xdef` now combines that expansion with grouped global persistence, `\gdef` now narrow-follows the same global definition path as grouped `\global\def`, `\expanded{...}` now reuses the same balanced-group full-expansion loop outside definition time, and that loop now honors `\protect`, `\noexpand`, makeatletter alias `\@nx`, and balanced-group `\unexpanded{...}` so literal control sequences or grouped token lists can survive to runtime while plain execution still treats `\protect` as a no-op; dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixtures pin those paths under later option-only revisions
  - protect-adjacent makeatletter aliases are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\@typeset@protect` now narrow-follows the same runtime no-op path as `\protect`, `\@unexpandable@protect` now narrow-follows the same `\edef`/`\xdef` noexpand path as `\protect`, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins those aliases under a later option-only revision
  - token inspection helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\meaning` now narrow-materializes primitive, macro, character, and undefined token meanings as conservative text instead of falling through as an undefined control sequence, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both direct output and `\edef` capture paths under a later option-only revision
  - token detokenization helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\detokenize{...}` now narrow-materializes balanced-group token lists without expanding their control sequences, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both direct output and `\edef` capture paths under a later option-only revision
  - token prefix-stripping helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\strip@prefix` now narrow-discards the leading `macro:->`-style prefix off `\meaning` output through the first `>` delimiter, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both direct output and `\edef` capture paths under a later option-only revision
  - token case-transform helpers are now also fixed and covered at the same preamble-definition level: `\uppercase` and `\lowercase` now narrow-transform only character tokens inside balanced groups while leaving control-sequence tokens for later runtime expansion, and a dedicated wrapper class/package corpus fixture pins both direct output and `\edef` capture paths under a later option-only revision
